# 297\n
{Edinburgh, Royal College of Physicians, MS of Cursor Mundi, hand A, fols. 1r-15v}\n
C14a\n
486 447 N\n
{=ERY=}\n
{=Sample represents all the English in this hand=}\n
{=Script - small compressed Textura=}\n
{=Status - MS punctuation done; tagging notes and textual notes up to date=}\n
{=The extracts from Cursor Mundi in this MS are imperfect and wrongly\n
ordered. Hand C provides the earlier portions, Cursor Mundi lines\n
18989-22417 (with gaps). Hand A provides lines 22418-24359, 24530-730,\n
24733-968. Between Hand A\'s and Hand C\'s contributions Hand B provides\n
some of the Northern Homily Collection. Hand A\'s contribution begins\n
in Morris\'s edition vol. 5 (EETS OS 68, 1878), Appendix 1, p. 1616 and\n
continues at vol. 5 p. 1367. The scribe\'s thorn is open-topped but quite\n
different in shape from <y>, which is also used quite extensively for\n
both [i] and [j], unlike Scribe C\'s habit. Punctuation is virtually\n
absent. Punctus on either side of capital <I> are taken to be part of\n
the figura and are ignored. Forms of majuscule and minuscule thorn,\n
<w> and <v> are identical in this hand. The majuscule forms of all\n
other letters are regularly used at the start of each verse line.\n
I have followed Morris in indicating capitals in this position for\n
thorn <w> and <v> also. In his edition, Morris expands the usual\n
abbreviation for <er> either as <ir> or <er> according to the word. Here\n
I always expand, as with our normal practice, as <er>. In hand C, the\n
same abbreviation (a hook above the preceding letter) is used after A as\n
an abbreviation for "and". Hand A also uses this hook abbreviation on A\n
for "and" though his <er> abbreviation is different - an upright zigzag\n
above the preceding letter. For "and" I follow what I did in language 2\n
of the Cotton Owl and the Nightingale and with Hand C of this MS, and\n
transcribe A~=}\n
{~f1ra~}\n
